AVON was incorporated and headquartered in New York, New York.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">2.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">At all times relevant to this Statement of Facts, AVON issued and maintained a class of publicly traded securities registered pursuant to Section 12(b) of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934 (15 U.S.C. &#167; 78</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;">l</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">) and was required to file periodic reports with the SEC under Section 13 of the Securities Exchange Act (15 U.S.C. &#167; 78m). Accordingly, AVON was an &#8220;issuer&#8221; within the meaning of the FCPA, Title 15, United States Code, Section 78dd-1.  AVON&#8217;s shares traded on the New York Stock Exchange under the symbol &#8220;AVP.&#8221;</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">3.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">At all times relevant to this Statement of Facts, Avon Products (China) Co. Ltd. (&#8220;Avon China&#8221;) was an indirect subsidiary of AVON incorporated in China. Avon China and its affiliates manufactured and sold beauty and healthcare products through direct sales, as well as through &#8220;beauty boutiques&#8221; that were independently owned and operated. In addition to its independent sales representatives, Avon China had between 1,000 and 2,000 employees. Avon China&#8217;s books, records, and accounts were consolidated into AVON&#8217;s books and records and reported by AVON in its financial statements.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">4.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">&#8220;Avon China Executive 1,&#8221; a Taiwanese citizen who resided in China, was a senior executive at Avon China from in or around 1999 through in or around April 2010.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">5.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">&#8220;Avon China Executive 2,&#8221; a Chinese citizen who resided in China, was a senior executive in Avon China&#8217;s Corporate Affairs, State Government, and Media Relations group (&#8220;Corporate Affairs Group&#8221;) from in or around 1999 through in or around April 2010. The Corporate Affairs Group consisted of approximately 40 employees, whose duties included lobbying government officials on behalf of Avon China.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 2</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="s67D044886348332C1F93532EEC574B25"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:4px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">6.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">At all times relevant to this Statement of Facts, &#8220;Consulting Company A,&#8221; was a Chinese company that purportedly provided government and public relations work for Avon China.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">7.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">&#8220;Avon Executive 1,&#8221; a United States citizen, was a senior executive in AVON&#8217;s Asia Pacific Region (which included China) and AVON&#8217;s China Region (during times it was not part of the Asia Pacific Region) from in or around 2002 to in or around February 2011.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">8.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">&#8220;Avon Executive 2,&#8221; a United States citizen, held a variety of positions at AVON from 1972 through April 2010, including a senior finance position in AVON&#8217;s Asia Pacific Region from in or around February 2005 to in or around May 2006. From in or around May 2006 through in or around February 2009, Avon Executive 2 was a senior executive in the internal audit group at AVON.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:50px;">9.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">&#8220;Avon Executive 3,&#8221; a United States citizen, was a senior executive in AVON&#8217;s internal audit group from in or around June 2003 to in or around February 2006.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">10.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">&#8220;Avon Attorney 1,&#8221; a United States citizen, was a senior executive in AVON&#8217;s Office of the General Counsel from in or around 2001 through in or around December 2007.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">11.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">&#8220;Avon Attorney 2,&#8221; a United States citizen, was an executive in AVON&#8217;s Office of the General Counsel from in or around 1993 to in or around August 2006. In that position, Avon Attorney 2 was responsible for providing legal advice to AVON&#8217;s international subsidiaries.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:50px;">12.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">&#8220;Avon Internal Auditor 1,&#8221; a dual Chinese and Canadian citizen, was an internal auditor at AVON from in or around August 2005 to in or around July 2008.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 3</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="s5BBC37CB56989FF6C7AE532EEC86F248"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:center;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">The Chinese Regulatory Regime for Direct Selling</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">13.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In or around 1998, the Chinese government outlawed direct selling in China for all companies.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">14.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In or around 2001, as a condition of its entry to the World Trade Organization, China agreed to lift its ban on direct selling. In or around 2005, in order to test its planned regulations for direct selling, the Chinese government decided to issue one company a temporary license to conduct direct sales (the &#8220;test license&#8221;).</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">15.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In or around March 2005, the Chinese government awarded the test license to Avon China.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">16.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In or around late 2005, China lifted its ban on direct selling and allowed companies to apply for licenses to conduct direct sales. Under China&#8217;s newly promulgated direct selling regulations, to conduct direct sales, a company was required to obtain a national direct selling license and approvals from each province and municipality in which it sought to conduct direct sales. In order to obtain a license, a company was required to satisfy a number of conditions, including, in pertinent part, having &#8220;a good business reputation&#8221; and a record that demonstrated no material violations of Chinese law for the preceding five years.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">17.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In or around February 2006, Avon China obtained its national direct selling license.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">18.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">Between in or around February 2006 and in or around July 2006, Avon China obtained all of its provincial and municipal approvals to conduct direct selling.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 4</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="s4FB10693F9EE94EB8653532EECB481EC"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:center;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">AVON&#8217;s Internal Controls</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">19.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">At all times relevant to this Statement of Facts, although AVON and certain of its subsidiaries had policies in place relating to the review and approval of employee expenses, it lacked adequate controls to ensure compliance with those policies and thus, in practice, employee expenses were not adequately vetted to ensure that they were reasonable, bona fide, or properly documented.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">20.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">At all times relevant to this Statement of Facts, AVON lacked sufficient controls to ensure the integrity of its internal audit process, particularly with regard to its review of allegations of and testing for improper payments made to foreign government officials. AVON&#8217;s internal audit group also failed to devote adequate funding, staffing, and resources to Avon  China.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">21.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">At all times relevant to this Statement of Facts, AVON did not have adequate internal accounting and financial controls designed to detect and prevent, among other things, corruption-related violations, including FCPA violations. In particular, after senior AVON executives, including Avon Executives 1, 2, and 3 and Avon Attorneys 1 and 2, learned of specific corruption issues in China related to the provision of cash, meals, gifts, travel, and entertainment to government officials, AVON failed to devote adequate resources to investigating such issues and to take the necessary steps to implement appropriate controls to address such issues and prevent such risks in the future.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;padding-right:48px;">22.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">At all times relevant to this Statement of Facts, AVON failed to implement accounting controls that would help ensure that transactions were executed and recorded in such a way as to maintain accountability for assets.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 5</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="sD998BFEC369A14413A20532EECE33356"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:4px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">23.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">At all times relevant to this Statement of Facts, AVON also had an inadequate compliance program. In fact, AVON did not have a dedicated compliance officer or compliance personnel. AVON&#8217;s compliance program was particularly weak with regard to risks associated with foreign bribery. For example, even though AVON operated in over 100 countries, including many countries with high corruption risks, AVON did not have a specific anti- corruption policy, nor did it provide stand-alone FCPA-related training. Moreover, although AVON had a code of conduct that covered all of its employees and its subsidiaries&#8217; employees, which, among other things, prohibited paying bribes, many employees of AVON and its subsidiaries were unaware of its existence.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">24.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">At all times relevant to this Statement of Facts, AVON did not conduct corruption-related due diligence on appropriate third parties or have effective controls for the meaningful approval process of third parties. AVON also did not require adequate documentation supporting the retention of or payments to third parties.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">25.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">Additionally, AVON did not undertake periodic risk assessments of its compliance program and lacked proper oversight of gifts, travel, and entertainment expenditures. AVON&#8217;s failure to maintain an adequate compliance program significantly contributed to the company&#8217;s failure to prevent the misconduct in China.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:141px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:center;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Overview of the Scheme to Falsify Books and Records</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">26.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">Due to AVON&#8217;s failure to implement effective internal accounting controls, AVON and Avon China executives and employees were able to &#8211; and did &#8211; falsely or misleadingly describe certain transactions on Avon China&#8217;s books and records, and thereby</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 6</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="s7E9FE003893B440B7BF7532EED02FA3C"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">ultimately, AVON&#8217;s books and records, in order to disguise things of value Avon China executives and employees had given to government officials in China.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">27.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">At all times relevant to this Statement of Facts, Avon China maintained a Corporate Affairs Group whose duties included maintaining &#8220;guanxi&#8221; (good relationships) with government officials and lobbying those officials on behalf of Avon China.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">28.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">Avon China, primarily through Avon China Executives 1 and 2, tasked its Corporate Affairs Group with lobbying government officials to enable Avon China to: (1) obtain a national license and requisite provincial and local approvals to conduct direct sales in China; (2) avoid government fines, the imposition of which Avon China executives and employees believed could cause Avon China to lose its direct selling license; (3) avoid negative media reports that could hurt Avon China&#8217;s image or cause it to be fined, thus endangering its direct selling license; (4) obtain favorable judicial treatment; and (5) obtain government approval to sell nutritional supplements and healthcare apparel products, via direct selling, that did not meet or had yet to meet government standards.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">29.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">Avon China&#8217;s Corporate Affairs Group engaged in a routine practice of giving things of value to Chinese government officials in order to carry out its assigned tasks. Additionally, other Avon China executives and employees also provided things of value to government officials to obtain business benefits for Avon China.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">30.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">Avon China Executive 2 instructed Corporate Affairs Group employees not to maintain accurate, detailed records of things of value, including cash, gifts, and non-business meals, entertainment, and travel, they gave to government officials in the course of carrying out their assigned tasks.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 7</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="s0AC766C1376473D0B3CF532EED31F98E"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:4px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">31.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">Avon China&#8217;s Corporate Affairs Group, and other Avon China executives and employees, intentionally falsified records and intentionally omitted information from records so as to conceal the things of value they provided to government officials.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">32.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">AVON and Avon China executives and employees knowingly concealed from other AVON executives and others that Avon China&#8217;s books and records failed to reflect accurately and fairly the nature and purpose of certain transactions, knowing that Avon China&#8217;s books and records would be consolidated into AVON&#8217;s books and records.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:center;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:center;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Details of the Scheme</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:center;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">33.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">From at least in or around 2004 through in or around September 2008, Avon China, acting through certain executives and employees, disguised on its books and records over</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:8px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">$8 million in things of value, including gifts, cash, and non-business travel, meals, and entertainment, which it gave to Chinese government officials in order to obtain and retain business benefits for Avon China.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">34.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">Avon China executives and employees falsely and misleadingly described the nature and purpose of certain transactions on Avon China&#8217;s books and records, in part, because they believed that Chinese government officials did not want a paper trail reflecting their acceptance of money, gifts, travel, entertainment and other things of value from Avon China executives and employees. The executives and employees also knew that, contrary to how the expenses were being described in Avon China&#8217;s books and records, the expenses were not incurred for legitimate business purposes.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;padding-right:48px;">35.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">In order to conceal its executives&#8217; and employees&#8217; practice of giving things of value to Chinese government officials, from at least in or around 2004 through in or around</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 8</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="s26A87E0CC20D4262472C532EED5074D7"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;padding-left:8px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">September 2008, Avon China executives and employees intentionally falsified certain transactions on Avon China&#8217;s books and records by, among other things, falsely describing expenses related to government officials as employee-related or falsely or misleadingly describing the nature or purpose of, or participants associated with, such expenses in order to conceal that the expenses related to government officials or that there were expectations of benefits from government officials. Additionally, Avon China executives and employees intentionally falsified Avon China&#8217;s books and records by falsely recording payments to Consulting Company A as payments for legitimate services, notwithstanding the fact that Avon China Executive 2 knew that Consulting Company A&#8217;s invoices were often false and no Avon China executives or employees knew of any legitimate services being provided by Consulting Company A.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">36.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">AVON executives and employees, including high-level executives, attorneys, and internal auditors, learned that executives and employees of Avon China had in the past routinely provided things of value to Chinese government officials and failed to properly document it. Instead of ensuring the practice was halted, disciplining the culpable individuals, and implementing appropriate controls at AVON and Avon China to address this problem, AVON executives and employees, in conjunction with Avon China executives and employees, took  steps to conceal the significant concerns raised about the accuracy of Avon China&#8217;s books and records and its practice of giving things of value to government officials. These AVON and Avon China executives and employees, knowing that Avon China&#8217;s books and records would continue to be inaccurate if steps were not taken to correct Avon China&#8217;s executives&#8217; and</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 9</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="sC765E7781580FBA05823532EED8FA2BC"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">employees&#8217; conduct, failed to take steps to correct such actions, despite knowing that Avon China&#8217;s books and records were consolidated into AVON&#8217;s books and records.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;text-decoration:underline;">Gifts for Government Officials</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:4px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">37.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">From in or around 2004 through in or around September 2008, Avon China executives and employees intentionally falsified Avon China&#8217;s books and records related to gifts given to Chinese government officials, including AVON products and personal luxury items like designer wallets, bags, or watches, to obtain benefits from government officials, such as obtaining and retaining the direct selling license and requisite provincial and local approvals, avoiding fines, avoiding negative media reports, obtaining favorable judicial treatment, and obtaining government approval to sell nutritional supplements and healthcare apparel products, via direct selling, that did not meet or had yet to meet government standards. At various times, Avon China executives and employees concealed in the books and records the actual purposes of the gifts, the identity of the recipients, or the price per gift. Also, Avon China executives and employees, at various times, falsely or misleadingly described the gifts, including describing  them as employee travel and entertainment, &#8220;samples,&#8221; or &#8220;public relations business entertainment.&#8221; Avon China executives and employees falsely or misleadingly described such expenses in order to conceal that gifts were given to government officials with an expectation of receiving a business benefit.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">38.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">For example, Avon China employees falsely or misleadingly described gifts as follows:</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:96px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">a.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In or around October 2006, Avon China employees falsely described approximately $890 of &#8220;gifts&#8221; for government officials as an &#8220;entertainment&#8221; expense, and</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 10</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="sAA70DE9140DC99FC4755532EED9E07D1"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;padding-left:8px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">omitted from the records the recipient of the gifts and the purpose of the gifts.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;text-align:left;text-indent:96px;"><font style="text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">b.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In or around March 2008, Avon China employees inaccurately described an approximately $960 gift purchased from Louis Vuitton for a government official as a a &#8220;public relations entertainment&#8221; expense, and omitted from the records the recipient of the gift and the purpose of the gift.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:96px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">c.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In or around July 2008, Avon China employees falsely described an approximately $800 Gucci bag given to a government official as a &#8220;business entertainment&#8221; expense, and omitted from the records the recipient of the bag and the purpose of the gift.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:96px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">d.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In or around July 2008, Avon China employees falsely described an approximately $460 gift from Louis Vuitton for a government official as a &#8220;Public Relation Business Entertainment&#8221; expense, and omitted from the records the recipient of the gift and the purpose of the gift.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:8px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;text-decoration:underline;">Meals and Entertainment</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:4px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">39.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">From in or around 2004 through in or around September 2008, Avon China executives and employees routinely entertained government officials in order to obtain specific business benefits, such as obtaining and retaining the direct selling license and requisite provincial and local approvals, avoiding fines, avoiding negative media reports, obtaining favorable judicial treatment, and obtaining government approval to sell nutritional supplements and healthcare apparel products, via direct selling, that did not meet or had yet to meet government standards.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">40.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">Indeed, in or around August 2005, Avon China Executives 1 and 2 created a &#8220;Direct Selling Special Task Force,&#8221; which was comprised primarily of employees from the</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 11</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="s96AE1AD2ACC2C6765080532EEDDDD66D"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;padding-left:8px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">Corporate Affairs Group, whose task was to obtain local and provincial direct selling approvals for Avon China through &#8220;relations,&#8221; which was a term Avon China executives and employees used to refer to things of value provided to government officials or goodwill that had been obtained by giving such things, including non-business meals and entertainment.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">41.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">Members of the Direct Selling Special Task Force and other Avon China executives and employees intentionally concealed improper meal and entertainment expenses in Avon China&#8217;s books and records by (1) intentionally omitting reference to the participation of government officials in order to conceal their participation, using descriptions like &#8220;business entertainment,&#8221; &#8220;public relation entertainment,&#8221; or no description at all; or (2) revealing the participation of government officials but intentionally describing the event inaccurately by omitting the identity or number of officials, the cost of the event, or the true purpose of the event.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">42.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">As a result, meal and entertainment expenses for government officials were falsely or misleadingly described on Avon China&#8217;s books, including the following expenses:</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;padding-left:8px;text-indent:96px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">a.&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;In or around 2006, Avon China employees falsely described as &#8220;sales- business entertainment&#8221; approximately $8,100 an Avon China executive spent on meals and entertainment provided to government officials in order to obtain government approval to sell a healthcare apparel product that did not meet government standards.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:8px;text-indent:96px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">b.&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;In or around January 2008, Avon China employees falsely described as &#8220;business entertainment&#8221; and employee &#8220;accommodation&#8221; expenses, approximately $3,206 spent on meals, entertainment, and lodging for government officials.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 12</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="s95B381B26BA391501DEF532EEDFC73CE"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;text-decoration:underline;">Travel for Government Officials</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:4px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">43.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">From in or around 2004 through in or around September 2008, Avon China executives and employees caused Avon China to pay for travel expenses for government officials, and sometimes their families, in order to obtain improper business benefits, including obtaining and retaining the direct selling license and requisite provincial and local approvals, avoiding fines, avoiding negative media reports, obtaining favorable judicial treatment, and obtaining government approval to sell nutritional supplements and healthcare apparel products, via direct selling, that did not meet or had yet to meet government standards. To conceal the true nature of these expenses, these executives and employees intentionally omitted from or  concealed in Avon China&#8217;s records the names of the government officials, the fact that the travelers were government officials or relatives of government officials, and, at times, the number of travelers.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">44.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">Avon China executives and employees also intentionally falsified in Avon  China&#8217;s books and records the purpose of the travel, which often was for personal, not legitimate business, purposes. For example, Avon China employees described personal trips for government officials (and occasionally their spouses and children) as &#8220;study trips&#8221; or &#8220;site visits&#8221; when the officials were instead sightseeing or taking a beach vacation.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">45.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">As a result, non-business travel expenses for government officials were falsely or misleadingly described on the books of Avon China, including the following expenses:</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;text-indent:96px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">a.&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;In or around December 2005, Corporate Affairs Group employees sought approval to take six officials from the Guandong Food and Drug Administration with responsibility for approving Avon China&#8217;s healthcare products for sale, to the United States,</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 13</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="s7E36D5E5B2B99A7816CF532EEE2B2A2C"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">purportedly for a &#8220;site visit/study visit&#8221; to AVON&#8217;s headquarters in New York City and its research and development facility in upstate New York.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;text-indent:96px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">b.&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;In or around September 2006, Avon China employees falsely described the approximately $90,000 Avon China spent on a trip for four of those officials in Avon China&#8217;s books and records as a business-related site visit and study trip for Chinese government officials, notwithstanding the fact that the officials never visited AVON&#8217;s headquarters, only spent one morning at AVON&#8217;s research and development facility, and spent the rest of the 18-day trip sightseeing and being entertained by an Avon China employee in New York, Vancouver, Montreal, Ottawa, Toronto, Philadelphia, Seattle, Las Vegas, Los Angeles, Hawaii, and Washington, DC.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;text-indent:96px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">c.&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;In or around January 2008, Avon China employees falsely described in Avon China&#8217;s books and records as a &#8220;site visit to Guangzhou&#8221; for &#8220;3 aic [Administration for Industry and Commerce] officials,&#8221; approximately $1,200 worth of expenses associated with a personal trip Avon China provided to a government official and the official&#8217;s spouse and child to Guangzhou and Macau.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;text-indent:96px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">d.&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;In or around January 2008, Avon China employees falsely described in Avon China&#8217;s books and records as &#8220;site visit/inspection&#8221; expenses approximately $15,400 Avon China paid for government officials to travel to Guangzhou, Shenzhen, and Sanya notwithstanding the fact that the underlying records include charges for a tour guide, sightseeing van, and items purchased at the beach.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;text-indent:96px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">e.&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;In or around February 2008, Avon China employees falsely described in Avon China&#8217;s books and records as &#8220;business entertainment&#8221; approximately $11,000 Avon</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 14</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="s3E22BCBE8863CB2F50A4532EEE5AD412"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">China paid for separate trips for two government officials who oversaw Avon China&#8217;s activities in the Shaanxi Province (and no Avon China employees) to take personal trips to celebrate the Chinese New Year; one, a 9-day personal trip to Hainan Island and the other, a 12-day personal trip that included stays in Hong Kong and Macau.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;text-decoration:underline;">Cash for Government Officials</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:4px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">46.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">From in or around 2004 through in or around September 2008, Avon China executives and employees gave cash to government officials and falsified Avon China&#8217;s records to conceal the true recipient of and purpose for the money.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">47.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In large part, these employees accomplished this by submitting for reimbursement meal or entertainment receipts given to them by government officials and falsely claiming that the receipts reflected employee business expenses. In truth, the employees had no such  expenses, and the receipts were used to obtain cash to make payments to government officials. On occasion, employees would falsely submit receipts for multiple meals on the same date, none of which the employees had actually attended.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">48.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In other instances, Corporate Affairs Group employees, and other Avon China executives and employees gave cash to government officials in order to obtain business benefits for Avon China and falsely reported the payments as fine payments. Avon China executives and employees also made payments to organizations designated by government officials in order to obtain business benefits for Avon China and intentionally omitted from Avon China&#8217;s records the true purpose of the payments.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 15</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="sFD2B8926624D06A3E54D532EEE88BBF2"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:4px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">49.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">Due to these practices, from in or around 2004 through in or around September 2008, cash given to government officials was falsely or misleadingly described on the books and records of Avon China.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">50.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">For example, Avon China employees falsely or misleadingly described the following cash payments to government officials:</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:56px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-left:48px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;text-decoration:underline;">Cash to Avoid a Fine</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;padding-left:8px;text-indent:96px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">a.&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;On or about August 16, 2006, Avon China Executive 2 approved a request from a Corporate Affairs Group employee to send RMB 100,000 (approximately $12,000) to a government official&#8217;s bank account to avoid a fine for violating China&#8217;s direct selling  regulations.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:8px;text-indent:96px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">b.&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;On or about August 17, 2006, to support the request for a RMB 100,000 payment to a government official, the requesting Corporate Affairs Group employee submitted a handwritten certificate, purportedly from a Chinese government agency, falsely stating that the official would give the funds to the government bureau.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:8px;text-indent:96px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">c.&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;On or about August 17, 2006, an Avon China employee caused RMB 100,000 to be wired in three separate wires to the government official&#8217;s personal bank account.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:8px;text-indent:96px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">d.&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;In or around late August 2006, an Avon China finance employee sent an email to an Avon China employee, who forwarded it to Avon China Executive 2, stating that &#8220;the company paid RMB 100,000 to [the Chinese government official] as compensation payment and now we need to enter it into the book.&#8221;</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:8px;text-indent:96px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">e.&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;In or around late August 2006, notwithstanding that the Avon China finance employees knew the payment to the government official was &#8220;compensation,&#8221; they</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 16</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="s5FC6E10B5A4508A5E268532EEEA8D364"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">recorded the payment in the &#8220;management expenses &#8211; government relations expenses&#8221; account   as a legitimate payment related to &#8220;issue of aic [Administration for Industry and Commerce] in [] county of [] province.&#8221;</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:54px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-left:48px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;text-decoration:underline;">Sponsorship to Avoid a Negative Media Article</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;text-indent:96px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">f.&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;In or around December 2006, Avon China Executive 2 expressed concern to the Corporate Affairs Group that an article a leading government-owned newspaper intended to run about Avon China improperly recruiting sales associates could cause Avon China to lose its direct selling license.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;text-indent:96px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">g.&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;In or around December 2006, in order to convince the newspaper not to run the article, a Corporate Affairs Group employee caused Avon China to pay approximately RMB 620,000 (approximately $77,500) to become a &#8220;sponsor&#8221; of the paper at the request of a government official at the paper who was in charge of determining whether the potential article would run and who may have received a commission on monies received from sponsors.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;text-indent:96px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">h.&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;In or around December 2006, a Corporate Affairs Group employee sent an internal email regarding the potential article, noting that the &#8220;the story alerted us to re-consider to invest more time and efforts on building key medium&#8217;s relationship. [The paper] is the one with responsibility to submit confidential memo to the State Counsel and release media story to public as well.&#8221;</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;text-decoration:underline;">Payments to Consulting Company A</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:4px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">51.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In or around October 2003, Avon China Executive 2 retained Consulting Company A purportedly to &#8220;provide the following services upon [Avon China&#8217;s] request: (1) crisis management; (2) government relations; and (3) coordinate with public security</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 17</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="s562D1993BAE8197D0E81532EEED61AFC"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">authorities.&#8221; In exchange for these services, which were memorialized in a scant two-page contract with Avon China, Avon China contracted to pay Consulting Company A $2,000 to $7,000 per month plus expenses.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">52.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">Avon China executives and employees did not conduct any due diligence on Consulting Company A, nor did they require Consulting Company A to comply with AVON&#8217;s Code of Conduct (in particular, the provisions related to payments to government officials), even though Consulting Company A was retained specifically to interact with government officials on behalf of Avon China.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">53.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">From in or around October 2003 through in or around September 2008, Avon China executives and employees caused Avon China to pay Consulting Company A additional monies for purportedly legitimate, though ambiguously described, services even though Avon China Executive 2 knew Consulting Company A&#8217;s invoices were often false, and no Avon China executives or employees knew of any legitimate services being provided by Consulting  Company A.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">54.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">For example, on or about June 1, 2005, Avon China employees falsely described approximately $43,000 that Avon China paid Consulting Company A as &#8220;PR Fees&#8221; and &#8220;sponsorship&#8221; in connection with a purported art exhibition, even though the exhibition never occurred.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">55.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">Additionally, in or around January 2008, Avon China employees falsely described as a legitimate government relations expense approximately $25,900 paid to Consulting  Company A purportedly for &#8220;communication service fee; business entertainment; transportation; hotel/lodging; telecommunications; material preparation&#8221; in connection with a threatened RMB</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 18</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="s6A382ED130C6619CB36A532EEEF6858F"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;padding-left:8px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">500,000 (approximately $66,000) fine for violating the direct selling regulations, even though no Avon China executives or employees knew of any legitimate services actually being performed by Consulting Company A.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">56.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">On many occasions from in or around October 2003 through in or around October 2005, Avon China Executive 2 delivered cash to Consulting Company A and then sought reimbursement from Avon China by submitting, or instructing the executive&#8217;s assistant to submit, Consulting Company A&#8217;s vague invoices that falsely described the expenses identified therein    as related to legitimate travel, entertainment, or public relations expenses.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:8px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;text-decoration:underline;">Discovery of the Falsification and Resulting Cover-Up</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:4px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">57.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">On or about June 2, 2005, a senior audit manager in AVON&#8217;s internal audit group reported to AVON&#8217;s Compliance Committee, which was comprised of several senior AVON executives, that Avon China executives and employees were not maintaining proper records of entertainment for government officials and that Avon China Executive 2 had explained that the practice was intentional because information regarding that entertainment was &#8220;quite sensitive.&#8221;</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:justify;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:justify;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">58.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In or around September 2005, AVON&#8217;s internal auditors audited the Corporate Affairs Group&#8217;s travel and entertainment and discretionary expenses and issued a draft report documenting their findings (referred to herein as the &#8220;Draft Audit Report&#8221;).</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">59.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">On or about September 29, 2005, Avon China Executive 2 told the internal audit team that Avon China executives and employees could not record the names of government officials who were given gifts or entertained or the purpose of the gifts or entertainment because government officials did not want their participation in these activities recorded and that if Avon</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 19</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="s70D7EBCEC5BB55245A3D532EEF24619F"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">China maintained such records, government officials would sever their ties with Avon China, which would harm Avon China&#8217;s business prospects.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:50px;">60.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">The Draft Audit Report, which was reviewed by Avon China Executives 1 and 2; Avon Executives 1, 2, and 3; Avon Attorneys 1 and 2; and others at AVON and Avon China, contained conclusions regarding the Corporate Affairs Group&#8217;s expenses including: (1) high value gifts and meals were offered to government officials on an ongoing basis; (2) the majority of the expenses related to gifts, meals, sponsorships, and travel of substantial monetary value for Chinese government officials to maintain relationships with the officials; (3) a third party consultant was paid a substantial sum of money to interact with the government but was not contractually required to follow the FCPA, was not actively monitored by Avon China, and was paid for vague and unknown services; and (4) the payments, and the lack of accurate, detailed records, may violate the FCPA or other anti-corruption laws.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">61.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">On or about September 29, 2005, Avon China&#8217;s management team, including Avon China Executives 1 and 2, insisted that the internal audit team remove the discussion of providing things of value to government officials and potential FCPA violations from the Draft Audit Report for fear that the report would be seen by Chinese government officials, other AVON or Avon China employees, or Avon China&#8217;s competitors.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">62.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">On or about September 29, 2005, Avon Executives 2 and 3 agreed with Avon China executives, including Avon China Executives 1 and 2, to delete the discussion of the Corporate Affairs Group&#8217;s conduct from the Draft Audit Report. Avon Executive 3 then directed the internal audit team to remove the language from the Draft Audit Report. Avon Executive 2 thereafter directed the internal audit team to either (1) retrieve every copy of the Draft Audit</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 20</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="sB6AA42F8647400FA5D94532EEF440561"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">Report and destroy them or (2) instruct the individuals who possessed copies of the Draft Audit Report to destroy them.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">63.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In or around October and November 2005, Avon Executives 1, 2, and 3, Avon Attorneys 1 and 2, and others gathered additional information regarding Avon China executives&#8217; and employees&#8217; practice of giving things of value to Chinese government officials. They also collected information showing a lack of FCPA controls.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">64.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In part, this information was gathered by Avon Internal Auditor 1, who was sent  to China to obtain additional information regarding things of value being provided to government officials and was instructed by Avon Executive 2 not to create any electronic records or send any emails when gathering this information, and not to use &#8220;FCPA&#8221; in any documents or emails. Avon Internal Auditor 1 gathered the requested information, which further documented the Corporate Affairs Group&#8217;s practice of giving things of value to government officials, and gave it to Avon Executive 2 on two handwritten sheets of paper. Avon Executive 2 then hand- carried the handwritten papers to AVON&#8217;s headquarters in New York, New York.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">65.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In or around November 2005, Avon China Executive 2 sent a letter to Avon China Executive 1, with a copy to Avon Executive 1 (Avon China Executive 2 also later forwarded the letter to Avon Attorney 2), stating:</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;padding-top:1px;text-align:justify;padding-left:54px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">no job security is very much disturbing due to the recent unrealistic questioning by GIA [global internal audit]. I am not against [&#8230;] auditing our expenses, but company&#8217;s policy should be reasonably flexible for us to work. We are not working for our interest, but for creating a favorable business environment for the company. CA department is like a fighting brigade, we are most of the time have to fight in a muddy field, if we get on our hands some dirt, it is not our fault! We should be much protected.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:justify;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 21</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="s0B7F0E10A2D57FFBAAD8532EEF827361"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:4px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">66.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In or around November 2005, Avon China Executive 2 sent another letter to Avon China Executive 1 expressing concern about Avon China Executive 2&#8217;s job because Avon China Executive 2 had to &#8220;work through some grey areas for the company&#8217;s best interest.&#8221; Avon China Executive 2 also stated concern that the Corporate Affairs Group would lose all of its &#8220;guanxi&#8221; (good relationships) if it was required to follow AVON&#8217;s rules regarding gifts and entertainment and maintain detailed records of the gifts and entertainment.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">67.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In or around December 2005, in light of the issues identified in the Draft Audit Report, Avon Executive 2 and Avon China Executive 2 discussed hiding at Avon China Executive 2&#8217;s house an off-book record with the names of recipients and details of the things of value provided to government officials. However, Avon China Executive 2 ultimately did not do so. Additionally, an AVON attorney with responsibility for the China region provided to Avon China Executive 2 FCPA compliance language to add to future contracts with Consulting Company A but that language was never added to the contract. However, AVON executives did not instruct any Avon China executives or employees to stop the conduct identified in the Draft Audit Report. Moreover, neither AVON nor Avon China executives or employees put in place controls to prevent the conduct or ensure the accuracy of Avon China&#8217;s books and records.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:8px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">68.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In or around December 2006, AVON&#8217;s internal auditors again reviewed the Corporate Affairs Group&#8217;s travel and entertainment and discretionary expenses and found that Corporate Affairs Group executives and employees were continuing their practice of giving things of value to government officials, were not accurately documenting the expenses (on or off site), and had still not incorporated FCPA compliance language in Consulting Company A&#8217;s contracts. Notwithstanding learning that the conduct was continuing and that Avon China&#8217;s</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 22</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="sD319F68872B8953D99C0532EEFD05955"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:240%;padding-top:4px;text-align:left;padding-left:6px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">books and records were still being falsified, no AVON or Avon China executives or employees took steps to stop or prevent the conduct from recurring, and Avon China executives and employees continued operating in the same improper manner.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:48px;">69.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">In or around January 2007, Avon Executive 2 reported to AVON&#8217;s Compliance Committee that the matter regarding potential FCPA violations by Avon China executives and employees had been closed as &#8220;unsubstantiated,&#8221; even though Avon Executive 2 and other AVON executives, attorneys, and employees knew of Avon China&#8217;s previous &#8211; and continuing &#8211; practice of giving things of value to government officials and the ongoing failure of Avon China&#8217;s books and records to reflect accurately and fairly the nature and purpose of certain transactions, as well as AVON&#8217;s and Avon China&#8217;s ongoing failure to implement internal controls to prevent such conduct from continuing in the future.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;padding-left:6px;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;text-indent:48px;"><font style="padding-top:1px;text-align:left;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:50px;">70.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">From in or around 2004 through in or around September 2008, to ensure the consolidation of Avon China&#8217;s false books and records into AVON&#8217;s books and records, Avon China executives, including Avon China Executive 1, signed false management representation letters to Avon China&#8217;s external auditor stating that Avon China&#8217;s books and records were fair and accurate.</font></div><div style="line-height:240%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><br><div style="text-align:center;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">A- 23</font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="sEE800B3A75ECC29E3514532EEFEF78D4"></a><div></div><br><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:center;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;font-weight:bold;">ATTACHMENT B</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:center;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;font-weight:bold;text-decoration:underline;">CERTIFICATE OF CORPORATE RESOLUTIONS</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:232%;padding-top:4px;text-align:justify;padding-left:8px;text-indent:53px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">WHEREAS, Avon Products, Inc. (the &#8220;Company&#8221;) has been engaged in discussions with the United States Department of Justice, Criminal Division, Fraud Section and the United States Attorney&#8217;s Office for the Southern District of New York (collectively the &#8220;Department&#8221;) regarding issues arising in relation to the Information charging conspiracy to violate the books and records provision of the Foreign Corrupt Practices Act (&#8220;FCPA&#8221;) and failure to implement internal accounting controls; and</font></div><div style="line-height:232%;padding-top:1px;text-align:justify;padding-left:8px;text-indent:53px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">WHEREAS, in order to resolve such discussions, it is proposed that the Company enter into a certain agreement with the Department; and</font></div><div style="line-height:232%;padding-top:1px;text-align:justify;padding-left:8px;text-indent:53px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">WHEREAS, the Company&#8217;s Senior Vice President, General Counsel &amp; Chief Ethics &amp; Compliance Officer of the Company, Jeff Benjamin, together with outside counsel for the Company, have advised the Board of Directors of the Company of its rights, possible defenses, the Sentencing Guidelines&#8217; provisions, and the consequences of entering into such agreement with the Department;</font></div><div style="line-height:232%;padding-top:1px;text-align:left;padding-left:61px;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">Therefore, the Board of Directors has RESOLVED that:</font></div><div style="line-height:232%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:232%;padding-left:8px;text-align:justify;text-indent:53px;"><font style="text-align:justify;font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;padding-right:46px;">1.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">The Company (a) acknowledges the filing of the two-count Information charging the Company with conspiracy to violate 15 U.S.C. &#167; 78m(b)(2)(A) in violation of 18 U.S.C. &#167; 371, and with criminal violation of 18 U.S.C. &#167;&#167; 78m(b)(2)(B), 78m(b)(5), and 78ff(a); (b) waives indictment on such charges and enters into a deferred
